Product Architecture\r\n\r\nThe Player experience must be divided into two primary layers.\r\n\r\n## 2.1 Player Library Layer\r\n\r\nThe Player Library is where Tall Tale cards belong.\r\n\r\nThe library should display Tall Tales grouped or filterable by state, including:\r\n\r\n* Invitations\r\n* Available Tall Tales\r\n* Tall Tales ready to begin\r\n* Tall Tales waiting for the Captain\r\n* Active Tall Tales\r\n* Tall Tales currently in progress\r\n* Paused Tall Tales\r\n* Completed Tall Tales\r\n* Historical sessions\r\n* Replayable Tall Tales\r\n* Archived Tall Tales, where applicable\r\n\r\nCards are allowed and encouraged in this layer.\r\n\r\nEach card represents a Tall Tale or session as a selectable adventure entry.\r\n\r\nPossible card actions include:\r\n\r\n* Accept Invitation\r\n* Decline Invitation\r\n* View Invitation\r\n* Begin Tall Tale\r\n* Join Lobby\r\n* Continue Adventure\r\n* Resume Session\r\n* Await Captain\r\n* View Completed Journal\r\n* Replay Tall Tale\r\n* View Session History\r\n\r\nThe cards must not be used as the primary in-session storytelling UI.\r\n\r\n## 2.2 Tall Tale Session Layer\r\n\r\nOnce the Player enters an active session, the application must use the immersive journal interface.\r\n\r\nThis applies to:\r\n\r\n* Newly started Tall Tales\r\n* Resumed Tall Tales\r\n* Joined Tall Tales\r\n* Invited Tall Tales after acceptance\r\n* Tall Tales already in progress\r\n* Reopened completed Tall Tales\r\n* Historical session playback\r\n* Replay sessions\r\n\r\nThe immersive journal must become the main visual and interaction surface.\r\n\r\nThe application must not simply show one content card at a time in the center of the screen.\r\n\r\nThe journal should feel like a physical adventure object that contains the Tall Tale.\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n# 3. Required Navigation Flow\r\n\r\nImplement a clear Player journey:\r\n\r\n```text\r\nRole Selection\r\n├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ Player Sign-In\r\n├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ Player Library\r\n├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ Select Tall Tale\r\n├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ Invitation or Lobby State\r\n├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ Enter Session\r\n├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ Immersive Journal Interface\r\n├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ Chapter Gameplay\r\n├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ Tall Tale Completion\r\n├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ Completed Journal Archive\r\n```\r\n\r\nThe application should support returning to the Player Library without destroying the active session.\r\n\r\nWhen the Player resumes, they should return to the correct journal state and page.\r\n\r\nRecommended route structure:\r\n\r\n```text\r\n/player\r\n/player/library\r\n/player/invitations\r\n\r\n/player/tall-tales/:tallTaleId\r\n/player/tall-tales/:tallTaleId/lobby\r\n\r\n/player/sessions/:sessionId\r\n/player/sessions/:sessionId/journal\r\n/player/sessions/:sessionId/map\r\n/player/sessions/:sessionId/artifacts\r\n/player/sessions/:sessionId/messages\r\n\r\n/player/history/:sessionId\r\n```\r\n\r\nThe exact route names may be adapted to the existing architecture, but the conceptual separation must remain.\r\n\r\nThe main Player session route should resolve to the immersive journal.\r\n\r\nFor example:\r\n\r\n```text\r\n/player/sessions/:sessionId\r\n```\r\n\r\nmay either directly render the journal or redirect to:\r\n\r\n```text\r\n/player/sessions/:sessionId/journal\r\n```\r\n\r\nDo not maintain multiple competing primary Player session interfaces.\r\n\r\nThere must be one canonical Tall Tale session shell.\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n# 4. Canonical Tall Tale Session Shell\r\n\r\nCreate or refactor a reusable Player Tall Tale Session shell.\r\n\r\nSuggested conceptual structure:\r\n\r\n```text\r\nPlayerTallTaleSessionShell\r\n├óŌĆØ┼ō├óŌĆØŌé¼├óŌĆØŌé¼ SessionEnvironment\r\n├óŌĆØ┼ō├óŌĆØŌé¼├óŌĆØŌé¼ TallTaleJournal\r\n├óŌĆØŌĆÜ   ├óŌĆØ┼ō├óŌĆØŌé¼├óŌĆØŌé¼ JournalCover\r\n├óŌĆØŌĆÜ   ├óŌĆØ┼ō├óŌĆØŌé¼├óŌĆØŌé¼ JournalSpread\r\n├óŌĆØŌĆÜ   ├óŌĆØŌĆÜ   ├óŌĆØ┼ō├óŌĆØŌé¼├óŌĆØŌé¼ LeftPage\r\n├óŌĆØŌĆÜ   ├óŌĆØŌĆÜ   ├óŌĆØŌĆØ├óŌĆØŌé¼├óŌĆØŌé¼ RightPage\r\n├óŌĆØŌĆÜ   ├óŌĆØ┼ō├óŌĆØŌé¼├óŌĆØŌé¼ PageTurnLayer\r\n├óŌĆØŌĆÜ   ├óŌĆØ┼ō├óŌĆØŌé¼├óŌĆØŌé¼ BindingLayer\r\n├óŌĆØŌĆÜ   ├óŌĆØ┼ō├óŌĆØŌé¼├óŌĆØŌé¼ BookmarkLayer\r\n├óŌĆØŌĆÜ   ├óŌĆØ┼ō├óŌĆØŌé¼├óŌĆØŌé¼ LoosePaperLayer\r\n├óŌĆØŌĆÜ   ├óŌĆØ┼ō├óŌĆØŌé¼├óŌĆØŌé¼ ArtifactLayer\r\n├óŌĆØŌĆÜ   ├óŌĆØ┼ō├óŌĆØŌé¼├óŌĆØŌé¼ MapLayer\r\n├óŌĆØŌĆÜ   ├óŌĆØ┼ō├óŌĆØŌé¼├óŌĆØŌé¼ SealLayer\r\n├óŌĆØŌĆÜ   ├óŌĆØŌĆØ├óŌĆØŌé¼├óŌĆØŌé¼ JournalInteractionLayer\r\n├óŌĆØ┼ō├óŌĆØŌé¼├óŌĆØŌé¼ LeftContextDrawer\r\n├óŌĆØ┼ō├óŌĆØŌé¼├óŌĆØŌé¼ RightContextDrawer\r\n├óŌĆØ┼ō├óŌĆØŌé¼├óŌĆØŌé¼ ObjectiveTray\r\n├óŌĆØ┼ō├óŌĆØŌé¼├óŌĆØŌé¼ SessionStatusLayer\r\n├óŌĆØ┼ō├óŌĆØŌé¼├óŌĆØŌé¼ CinematicLayer\r\n├óŌĆØ┼ō├óŌĆØŌé¼├óŌĆØŌé¼ HintLayer\r\n├óŌĆØ┼ō├óŌĆØŌé¼├óŌĆØŌé¼ NotificationLayer\r\n├óŌĆØŌĆØ├óŌĆØŌé¼├óŌĆØŌé¼ AccessibilityControls\r\n```\r\n\r\nNames may differ based on the current framework, but responsibilities should be separated cleanly.\r\n\r\nDo not build the journal as one enormous component containing routing, networking, rendering, animation, persistence, audio, and UI state in a single file.\r\n\r\nSeparate:\r\n\r\n* Session data\r\n* Page content\r\n* Animation state\r\n* Navigation state\r\n* Captain-triggered events\r\n* Player-triggered events\r\n* Historical mode\r\n* Accessibility mode\r\n* Visual rendering\r\n* Audio behavior\r\n* Loading and error states\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n# 5. Reuse the Existing Book Interface\r\n\r\nThe previously designed book-centered interface must be reused wherever technically reasonable.\r\n\r\nDo not replace it with:\r\n\r\n* A generic white modal\r\n* A plain card\r\n* A basic two-column layout\r\n* A standard dashboard\r\n* A flat EPUB reader\r\n* A list of chapter cards\r\n* A slideshow\r\n* A simple page with ├óŌé¼┼ōPrevious├óŌé¼┬Ø and ├óŌé¼┼ōNext├óŌé¼┬Ø buttons\r\n\r\nThe book must remain physically and visually central.\r\n\r\nPreserve and improve existing visual work such as:\r\n\r\n* Journal cover\r\n* Leather or aged material\r\n* Worn paper\r\n* Physical page thickness\r\n* Left and right page geometry\r\n* Center binding\r\n* Page curl\r\n* Page turn animation\r\n* Shadows\r\n* Ink\r\n* Handwritten annotations\r\n* Sketches\r\n* Maps\r\n* Bookmarks\r\n* Loose notes\r\n* Wax seals\r\n* Latch or clasp\r\n* Artifact placements\r\n* Environmental lighting\r\n* Background atmosphere\r\n\r\nIf the existing implementation contains visual defects, fix them during integration rather than deleting the feature.\r\n\r\nKnown quality expectations include:\r\n\r\n* The left side must use a true left-hand page asset or geometry.\r\n* The right side must use a true right-hand page asset or geometry.\r\n* Do not mirror or duplicate two right-hand pages.\r\n* The center binding must feel structurally part of the book.\r\n* The binding must not appear pasted above page-turn animations.\r\n* The binding must not incorrectly show through flipping pages.\r\n* No fixed rectangular overlays should remain visible through moving pages.\r\n* Page edges should look worn, irregular, and physically aged.\r\n* Page turns should include believable curvature and thickness.\r\n* The journal should be capable of beginning closed when the scene calls for it.\r\n* The cover-opening sequence must be preserved.\r\n* The latch or clasp should behave like a real attached object.\r\n* Wax seal animations should look physically believable.\r\n* Avoid perfectly straight, artificial break lines.\r\n* Avoid instant or cheap-looking transitions.\r\n* Reloading should restore correct session state instead of always replaying the wrong intro state.\r\n\r\nDo not regress existing animation work.\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n# 6. The Journal Is a Runtime Renderer for Creator Content\r\n\r\nThe journal must render the Tall Tale content created in the Creator or Studio interface.\r\n\r\nThe Creator should define the content and sequence.\r\n\r\nThe Player journal should interpret and present that content immersively.\r\n\r\nThe journal should support multiple block types.\r\n\r\nAt minimum, prepare the system for the following content modes.\r\n\r\n## 6.1 Story Page\r\n\r\nDisplays narrative content across one or both pages.\r\n\r\nSupports:\r\n\r\n* Title\r\n* Body text\r\n* Captain journal writing\r\n* Handwritten notes\r\n* Illustrations\r\n* Background art\r\n* Page stains\r\n* Margin annotations\r\n* Dates\r\n* Location names\r\n* Character names\r\n* Optional voiceover\r\n* Optional ambient audio\r\n* Optional animated ink\r\n* Optional delayed text appearance\r\n* Optional automatic page turn\r\n\r\n## 6.2 Riddle Page\r\n\r\nDisplays a clue or riddle.\r\n\r\nSupports:\r\n\r\n* Main riddle text\r\n* Emphasized words\r\n* Hidden symbols\r\n* Scribbled annotations\r\n* Illustration references\r\n* Location clues\r\n* Optional hint levels\r\n* Optional Captain reveal\r\n* Optional answer entry\r\n* Optional ├óŌé¼┼ōmark solved├óŌé¼┬Ø action\r\n* Optional automatic progression after Captain confirmation\r\n\r\n## 6.3 Map Page\r\n\r\nDisplays a Tall Tale map across one or both pages.\r\n\r\nSupports:\r\n\r\n* Map image\r\n* Markers\r\n* Hidden and revealed regions\r\n* Routes\r\n* Compass elements\r\n* Location labels\r\n* Animated route drawing\r\n* Newly revealed islands or destinations\r\n* Current objective marker\r\n* Discovered locations\r\n* Captain-triggered map changes\r\n\r\n## 6.4 Artifact Reveal\r\n\r\nDisplays a discovered object, modified image, animation, or visual reveal.\r\n\r\nSupports:\r\n\r\n* Static image\r\n* Animated image\r\n* Video or cinematic\r\n* Layered illustration\r\n* Object description\r\n* Artifact name\r\n* Discovery timestamp\r\n* Discovery location\r\n* Story significance\r\n* Captain-triggered reveal\r\n* Player acknowledgment\r\n* Collection state\r\n\r\nThis should be prepared for future augmented or screen-vision-assisted verification.\r\n\r\nDo not tightly couple artifact reveal logic to manual Captain controls.\r\n\r\nUse a trigger abstraction that can later accept events from:\r\n\r\n* Captain action\r\n* Automated rule\r\n* Location verification\r\n* Screen vision helper\r\n* External helper application\r\n* Future machine-learning recognition\r\n* Timed sequence\r\n\r\n## 6.5 Decision Page\r\n\r\nDisplays a Player choice.\r\n\r\nSupports:\r\n\r\n* Two or more options\r\n* Locked or unavailable options\r\n* Physical-looking choice presentation\r\n* Notes\r\n* Symbols\r\n* Pinned papers\r\n* Torn scraps\r\n* Carved markings\r\n* Consequence preview, if allowed\r\n* Hidden consequence, if configured\r\n* Captain approval, if required\r\n* Persistent decision storage\r\n\r\n## 6.6 Objective Page\r\n\r\nDisplays the current task.\r\n\r\nSupports:\r\n\r\n* Objective title\r\n* Objective description\r\n* Completion condition\r\n* Sub-objectives\r\n* Progress\r\n* Optional timer\r\n* Optional failure state\r\n* Optional recovery instructions\r\n* Captain override\r\n* Player confirmation\r\n* Automated completion event\r\n\r\n## 6.7 Location Verification Page\r\n\r\nWaits for the Player to reach or verify a location.\r\n\r\nSupports:\r\n\r\n* Pending state\r\n* Manual Captain confirmation\r\n* Player-submitted confirmation\r\n* Future screen vision event\r\n* Future helper application event\r\n* Failure state\r\n* Retry state\r\n* Hint release\r\n* Emergency Captain bypass\r\n\r\n## 6.8 Message or Letter Page\r\n\r\nDisplays a communication as a physical object.\r\n\r\nSupports:\r\n\r\n* Loose page\r\n* Folded note\r\n* Wax-sealed letter\r\n* Torn message\r\n* Bottle message\r\n* Captain communication\r\n* Character communication\r\n* Timed reveal\r\n* Read or unread state\r\n\r\n## 6.9 Cinematic Page\r\n\r\nTemporarily expands content beyond the journal.\r\n\r\nSupports:\r\n\r\n* Full-screen or environment-wide animation\r\n* Transition from book page into visual scene\r\n* Narration\r\n* Music\r\n* Animated text\r\n* Artifact reveal\r\n* Chapter intro\r\n* Chapter finale\r\n* Final Tall Tale revelation\r\n\r\nThe book must remain conceptually connected to the scene, even when content temporarily expands beyond its physical pages.\r\n\r\n## 6.10 Chapter Completion Page\r\n\r\nDisplays a major milestone.\r\n\r\nSupports:\r\n\r\n* Chapter title\r\n* Completion message\r\n* Updated map\r\n* New bookmark\r\n* New journal entry\r\n* Released content\r\n* Artifact summary\r\n* Player decisions\r\n* Captain note\r\n* Transition to next chapter\r\n* Session pause\r\n* Tall Tale completion\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n# 7. Content-Block Contract\r\n\r\nCreate or formalize a typed content-block contract.\r\n\r\nExample conceptual structure:\r\n\r\n```ts\r\ntype TallTaleContentBlock =\r\n  | StoryBlock\r\n  | RiddleBlock\r\n  | MapBlock\r\n  | ArtifactRevealBlock\r\n  | DecisionBlock\r\n  | ObjectiveBlock\r\n  | LocationVerificationBlock\r\n  | MessageBlock\r\n  | CinematicBlock\r\n  | ChapterCompleteBlock;\r\n```\r\n\r\nEach block should have shared metadata such as:\r\n\r\n```ts\r\ninterface BaseTallTaleBlock {\r\n  id: string;\r\n  tallTaleId: string;\r\n  chapterId: string;\r\n  type: TallTaleBlockType;\r\n  order: number;\r\n  title?: string;\r\n  visibility: \"hidden\" | \"locked\" | \"released\" | \"completed\";\r\n  releaseRule?: ReleaseRule;\r\n  completionRule?: CompletionRule;\r\n  captainControlled?: boolean;\r\n  skippable?: boolean;\r\n  replayable?: boolean;\r\n  journalPresentation?: JournalPresentationConfig;\r\n  createdAt: string;\r\n  updatedAt: string;\r\n}\r\n```\r\n\r\nJournal presentation configuration should allow each block to specify things such as:\r\n\r\n```ts\r\ninterface JournalPresentationConfig {\r\n  spreadMode?: \"left\" | \"right\" | \"two-page\" | \"overlay\" | \"cinematic\";\r\n  pageTemplate?: string;\r\n  paperStyle?: string;\r\n  inkStyle?: string;\r\n  transitionIn?: string;\r\n  transitionOut?: string;\r\n  pageTurnBehavior?: \"manual\" | \"automatic\" | \"captain-triggered\" | \"locked\";\r\n  ambientAudio?: string;\r\n  soundEffect?: string;\r\n  backgroundScene?: string;\r\n  bookmarkStyle?: string;\r\n  loosePaperStyle?: string;\r\n  sealStyle?: string;\r\n}\r\n```\r\n\r\nAdapt this to existing project conventions.\r\n\r\nDo not duplicate the Creator content model separately for the Player renderer.\r\n\r\nThe Creator and Player must use the same underlying canonical Tall Tale content data.\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n# 8. Session State Model\r\n\r\nThe Player journal must be driven by a persistent Tall Tale Session.\r\n\r\nA Tall Tale definition and a Tall Tale session must remain separate concepts.\r\n\r\n## 8.1 Tall Tale Definition\r\n\r\nRepresents authored content.\r\n\r\nContains:\r\n\r\n* Tall Tale metadata\r\n* Chapters\r\n* Content blocks\r\n* Rules\r\n* Assets\r\n* Default settings\r\n* Available roles\r\n* Creator information\r\n* Version information\r\n\r\n## 8.2 Tall Tale Session\r\n\r\nRepresents a particular playthrough.\r\n\r\nContains:\r\n\r\n* Session ID\r\n* Tall Tale ID\r\n* Tall Tale version\r\n* Captain ID\r\n* Player IDs\r\n* Invitation states\r\n* Session status\r\n* Current chapter\r\n* Current content block\r\n* Released blocks\r\n* Completed blocks\r\n* Player decisions\r\n* Discovered artifacts\r\n* Hints used\r\n* Captain overrides\r\n* Session events\r\n* Start time\r\n* Pause time\r\n* Completion time\r\n* Last activity time\r\n* Historical snapshot information\r\n\r\nRecommended session states include:\r\n\r\n```text\r\ndraft\r\ninviting\r\nlobby\r\nready\r\nstarting\r\nactive\r\nwaiting_for_player\r\nwaiting_for_captain\r\npaused\r\ncompleted\r\nabandoned\r\narchived\r\n```\r\n\r\nRecommended block progress states include:\r\n\r\n```text\r\nhidden\r\nlocked\r\navailable\r\nactive\r\nawaiting_input\r\nawaiting_verification\r\ncompleted\r\nfailed\r\nskipped\r\n```\r\n\r\nDo not use UI card state as the source of truth.\r\n\r\nThe session model must control the UI.\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n# 9. Shared Player and Captain Session\r\n\r\nThe Player and Captain must access the same Tall Tale session through different interfaces.\r\n\r\n## 9.1 Player Interface\r\n\r\nThe Player sees:\r\n\r\n* Released story content\r\n* Current chapter\r\n* Current objective\r\n* Journal pages\r\n* Available clues\r\n* Discovered artifacts\r\n* Allowed hints\r\n* Map progress\r\n* Party members\r\n* Session status\r\n* Completed content\r\n* Historical record\r\n\r\nThe Player must not see:\r\n\r\n* Unreleased future content\r\n* Hidden answers\r\n* Captain-only notes\r\n* Secret triggers\r\n* Recovery controls\r\n* Unreleased artifacts\r\n* Internal condition logic\r\n* Debug information\r\n\r\n## 9.2 Captain Interface\r\n\r\nThe Captain sees and controls:\r\n\r\n* Current Player position\r\n* Current chapter\r\n* Current content block\r\n* Released content\r\n* Locked content\r\n* Player progress\r\n* Trigger controls\r\n* Artifact reveal controls\r\n* Hint controls\r\n* Verification controls\r\n* Map reveal controls\r\n* Message release controls\r\n* Chapter completion controls\r\n* Session pause and resume\r\n* Emergency recovery\r\n* Skip or bypass controls\r\n* Player decisions\r\n* Session event timeline\r\n\r\nCaptain controls must update the Player journal through the shared session state.\r\n\r\nExamples:\r\n\r\nWhen the Captain releases a page:\r\n\r\n* The Player receives a session event.\r\n* The journal shows a physical response.\r\n* A bookmark may appear.\r\n* A seal may break.\r\n* Ink may write itself.\r\n* A loose note may slide into view.\r\n* The page may unlock.\r\n* The book may turn automatically.\r\n* A subtle notification may call attention to the new content.\r\n\r\nDo not merely refresh the entire page and abruptly replace the content.\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n# 10. Real-Time Synchronization\r\n\r\nUse the project├óŌé¼Ōäós existing synchronization mechanism if one exists.\r\n\r\nPreferred options include:\r\n\r\n* WebSockets\r\n* Server-Sent Events\r\n* Event streaming\r\n* Structured polling as a fallback\r\n\r\nDo not introduce multiple redundant synchronization systems unlesŌĆ”24 tokens truncatedŌĆ”tely from canonical session progress.\r\n\r\nCanonical session progress includes:\r\n\r\n* Current active block\r\n* Released content\r\n* Completed content\r\n* Decisions\r\n* Artifacts\r\n* Chapter progress\r\n\r\nPlayer reading state may include:\r\n\r\n* Last viewed page\r\n* Open drawer\r\n* Selected map layer\r\n* Current zoom\r\n* Read or unread page state\r\n* Audio preference\r\n* Reduced motion setting\r\n\r\nDo not let a Player manually browsing an old page change the canonical active block.\r\n\r\nThe journal should be able to show:\r\n\r\n* The active session position\r\n* The Player├óŌé¼Ōäós temporary reading position\r\n\r\nProvide a clear ├óŌé¼┼ōReturn to Current Objective├óŌé¼┬Ø action when the Player browses away from the live page.\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n# 20. Authorization and Visibility\r\n\r\nEnforce authorization on the backend and frontend.\r\n\r\nA Player may access a session only when:\r\n\r\n* Invited\r\n* Added to the Tall Tale\r\n* Participating in the session\r\n* Authorized to view a completed historical session\r\n\r\nDo not rely on hidden UI alone.\r\n\r\nValidate session access server-side.\r\n\r\nBlock visibility must also be server-controlled.\r\n\r\nThe Player API must not send secret unreleased content and merely hide it with CSS.\r\n\r\nCaptain-only data must not be included in Player payloads.\r\n\r\nCreate separate view models or serializers where needed.\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n# 21. Accessibility\r\n\r\nThe journal must remain usable despite its visual complexity.\r\n\r\nImplement:\r\n\r\n* Keyboard navigation\r\n* Visible focus states\r\n* Semantic buttons\r\n* Screen-reader labels\r\n* Reduced motion\r\n* Text scaling\r\n* Contrast-safe text\r\n* Alternative text for illustrations\r\n* Captions or transcripts for audio\r\n* Non-audio indicators for sound cues\r\n* Non-color indicators for status\r\n* Page number announcements\r\n* Current objective announcements\r\n* New content announcements\r\n* Focus management after page turns\r\n* Focus management after overlays open\r\n* Escape key handling for overlays\r\n\r\nFor screen readers, expose journal content in a logical reading order.\r\n\r\nDo not force assistive technology to interpret decorative page layers.\r\n\r\nDecorative elements should be hidden from the accessibility tree.\r\n\r\nThe visual journal may be physically two-page, but the semantic order must remain coherent.\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n# 22. Performance\r\n\r\nThe journal may be animation-heavy, but it must remain responsive.\r\n\r\nOptimize:\r\n\r\n* Large textures\r\n* Videos\r\n* Transparent assets\r\n* Page-turn layers\r\n* Off-screen content\r\n* Historical pages\r\n* Map assets\r\n* Artifact images\r\n* Audio\r\n\r\nUse:\r\n\r\n* Asset preloading for adjacent pages\r\n* Lazy loading for distant content\r\n* Cached session data\r\n* Memoized or isolated rendering where useful\r\n* GPU-friendly transforms\r\n* Controlled layer counts\r\n* Clean animation teardown\r\n\r\nAvoid:\r\n\r\n* Re-rendering the entire journal on every session event\r\n* Loading every Tall Tale asset at session start\r\n* Keeping dozens of full-resolution pages mounted\r\n* Unbounded event listeners\r\n* Leaking animation frames\r\n* Unbounded session event arrays in live memory\r\n\r\nProvide a graceful lower-performance mode if the existing project already supports quality settings.\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n# 23. API and Backend Requirements\r\n\r\nReview the current backend before creating new endpoints.\r\n\r\nExtend existing APIs where possible.\r\n\r\nPotential Player session endpoints:\r\n\r\n```text\r\nGET /api/player/tall-tales\r\nGET /api/player/invitations\r\nPOST /api/player/invitations/:invitationId/accept\r\nPOST /api/player/invitations/:invitationId/decline\r\n\r\nGET /api/player/sessions/:sessionId\r\nGET /api/player/sessions/:sessionId/journal\r\nGET /api/player/sessions/:sessionId/events\r\nGET /api/player/sessions/:sessionId/artifacts\r\nGET /api/player/sessions/:sessionId/map\r\n\r\nPOST /api/player/sessions/:sessionId/decisions\r\nPOST /api/player/sessions/:sessionId/objectives/:objectiveId/confirm\r\nPOST /api/player/sessions/:sessionId/hints/:hintId/request\r\nPOST /api/player/sessions/:sessionId/pages/:pageId/read\r\n```\r\n\r\nPotential Captain endpoints:\r\n\r\n```text\r\nGET /api/captain/sessions/:sessionId\r\nPOST /api/captain/sessions/:sessionId/start\r\nPOST /api/captain/sessions/:sessionId/pause\r\nPOST /api/captain/sessions/:sessionId/resume\r\nPOST /api/captain/sessions/:sessionId/blocks/:blockId/release\r\nPOST /api/captain/sessions/:sessionId/blocks/:blockId/complete\r\nPOST /api/captain/sessions/:sessionId/hints/:hintId/release\r\nPOST /api/captain/sessions/:sessionId/artifacts/:artifactId/reveal\r\nPOST /api/captain/sessions/:sessionId/locations/:locationId/verify\r\nPOST /api/captain/sessions/:sessionId/chapters/:chapterId/complete\r\nPOST /api/captain/sessions/:sessionId/override\r\n```\r\n\r\nThese routes are illustrative.\r\n\r\nMatch the project├óŌé¼Ōäós existing API conventions.\r\n\r\nDo not create duplicate endpoints if equivalent functionality already exists.\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n# 24. Data Migration\r\n\r\nIf existing sessions currently store card-based progression, migrate them to the new canonical session model without losing data.\r\n\r\nPreserve:\r\n\r\n* Existing Tall Tales\r\n* Existing Players\r\n* Existing Captains\r\n* Existing invitations\r\n* Existing active sessions\r\n* Existing completion progress\r\n* Existing chapter progress\r\n* Existing content blocks\r\n* Existing artifacts\r\n* Existing timestamps\r\n* Existing historical records\r\n\r\nWrite database migrations where required.\r\n\r\nMigrations must be:\r\n\r\n* Reversible where practical\r\n* Safe on existing data\r\n* Idempotent where appropriate\r\n* Tested\r\n* Documented\r\n\r\nDo not reset active Tall Tale sessions merely because the UI architecture is changing.\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n# 25. Remove Competing In-Session Card UI\r\n\r\nOnce the journal route is working and verified:\r\n\r\n* Remove or repurpose the current card-by-card gameplay interface.\r\n* Do not leave users able to enter two different Player gameplay experiences for the same session.\r\n* Cards may remain inside the Player Library.\r\n* Cards may remain in the lobby.\r\n* Cards may remain in Captain management views.\r\n* Cards may remain in Creator Studio.\r\n* Cards must not remain the canonical active Player Tall Tale experience.\r\n\r\nIf some card components contain useful content rendering logic, extract the data logic and reuse it inside journal renderers.\r\n\r\nDo not visually embed the old card interface inside the book.\r\n\r\nA rectangle pasted onto a parchment page is not integration. It is hostage-taking.\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n# 26. Testing Requirements\r\n\r\nAdd or update automated tests.\r\n\r\n## 26.1 Routing Tests\r\n\r\nVerify:\r\n\r\n* Library card opens the correct session.\r\n* Active session opens the journal.\r\n* Completed session opens historical journal mode.\r\n* Unauthorized Player cannot access session.\r\n* Invitation state routes correctly.\r\n* Waiting state routes correctly.\r\n* Reload restores the session.\r\n* Return to library preserves session.\r\n\r\n## 26.2 Session Tests\r\n\r\nVerify:\r\n\r\n* Current chapter is restored.\r\n* Current block is restored.\r\n* Released content is visible.\r\n* Locked content is hidden.\r\n* Captain-only content is never included.\r\n* Player decision persists.\r\n* Artifact discovery persists.\r\n* Hint release updates Player.\r\n* Chapter completion updates journal.\r\n* Tall Tale completion enters historical mode.\r\n\r\n## 26.3 Journal Rendering Tests\r\n\r\nVerify each block type:\r\n\r\n* Story\r\n* Riddle\r\n* Map\r\n* Artifact\r\n* Decision\r\n* Objective\r\n* Location verification\r\n* Message\r\n* Cinematic\r\n* Chapter completion\r\n\r\nVerify:\r\n\r\n* Single-page rendering\r\n* Two-page rendering\r\n* Page parity\r\n* First page\r\n* Last page\r\n* Locked pages\r\n* Unread pages\r\n* Historical mode\r\n* Active mode\r\n\r\n## 26.4 Animation Tests\r\n\r\nVerify:\r\n\r\n* No double page turns\r\n* No page index corruption\r\n* No binding overlay corruption\r\n* No persistent overlay through page turns\r\n* Cover state restores correctly\r\n* Reduced motion works\r\n* Reconnection does not replay completed triggers\r\n* Captain release triggers one animation\r\n\r\n## 26.5 Responsive Tests\r\n\r\nTest:\r\n\r\n* Large desktop\r\n* Standard laptop\r\n* Small laptop\r\n* Tablet landscape\r\n* Tablet portrait\r\n* Mobile portrait\r\n* Mobile landscape\r\n\r\n## 26.6 Accessibility Tests\r\n\r\nVerify:\r\n\r\n* Keyboard page navigation\r\n* Overlay focus trapping\r\n* Focus return\r\n* Screen-reader labels\r\n* Logical reading order\r\n* Reduced motion\r\n* Contrast\r\n* Alternative text\r\n* New content announcement\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n# 27. Manual Acceptance Scenarios\r\n\r\nThe implementation is not complete until the following scenarios work manually.\r\n\r\n## Scenario A: New Player Invitation\r\n\r\n1. Captain invites Player.\r\n2. Player sees invitation card in library.\r\n3. Player accepts invitation.\r\n4. Player enters lobby.\r\n5. Captain starts session.\r\n6. Player transitions into immersive journal.\r\n7. Journal begins at the first Tall Tale content.\r\n8. Captain releases the next page.\r\n9. Journal responds physically and displays the released content.\r\n\r\n## Scenario B: Resume Active Tall Tale\r\n\r\n1. Player leaves during an active chapter.\r\n2. Session remains active.\r\n3. Player returns to library.\r\n4. Card says ├óŌé¼┼ōContinue Adventure.├óŌé¼┬Ø\r\n5. Player selects card.\r\n6. Journal opens at correct chapter and block.\r\n7. Previous decisions and artifacts remain present.\r\n8. Intro sequence is not incorrectly replayed.\r\n\r\n## Scenario C: Captain-Controlled Artifact Reveal\r\n\r\n1. Player reaches artifact objective.\r\n2. Journal displays waiting state.\r\n3. Captain confirms discovery.\r\n4. Player receives session event.\r\n5. Artifact reveal animation plays.\r\n6. Artifact is added to collection.\r\n7. Journal progression advances.\r\n8. Reload preserves the artifact.\r\n\r\n## Scenario D: Completed Tall Tale\r\n\r\n1. Final chapter is completed.\r\n2. Completion sequence plays.\r\n3. Session becomes completed.\r\n4. Player returns to library.\r\n5. Card says ├óŌé¼┼ōOpen Completed Journal.├óŌé¼┬Ø\r\n6. Player opens it.\r\n7. Same journal interface appears in read-only historical mode.\r\n8. Player can browse all discovered content.\r\n9. Hidden unreleased content remains unavailable.\r\n10. Historical content is not altered by later Tall Tale edits.\r\n\r\n## Scenario E: Connection Loss\r\n\r\n1. Player is reading an active page.\r\n2. Connection is interrupted.\r\n3. Journal shows a tasteful reconnecting state.\r\n4. Connection resumes.\r\n5. Session state is refreshed.\r\n6. No duplicate event animations occur.\r\n7. Player remains on a valid page.\r\n8. Current objective remains accurate.\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n# 28. Visual Acceptance Criteria\r\n\r\nThe result must clearly satisfy all of the following:\r\n\r\n* The book is the dominant visual element during gameplay.\r\n* The interface does not resemble a dashboard.\r\n* The interface does not resemble a sequence of generic cards.\r\n* The journal looks physically layered.\r\n* The left and right pages are geometrically correct.\r\n* The center binding behaves correctly during page turns.\r\n* Pages do not clip through fixed overlays.\r\n* The journal can open, close, turn pages, reveal inserts, and show artifacts.\r\n* Supporting controls remain secondary.\r\n* Session status is understandable without breaking immersion.\r\n* The Player can always determine the current objective.\r\n* Historical sessions still feel like preserved adventures.\r\n* The experience remains usable with reduced motion and keyboard navigation.\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n# 29. Technical Quality Requirements\r\n\r\nFollow existing project conventions for:\r\n\r\n* Language\r\n* Framework\r\n* State management\r\n* API client\r\n* Routing\r\n* Styling\r\n* Testing\r\n* Database access\r\n* Error handling\r\n* Logging\r\n* Formatting\r\n* Linting\r\n* Build tooling\r\n\r\nDo not introduce a new major framework solely for this feature.\r\n\r\nDo not rebuild the entire project.\r\n\r\nDo not duplicate canonical data models.\r\n\r\nDo not use placeholder mock data in the final connected implementation.\r\n\r\nTemporary mock data is allowed only during isolated component development and must be removed before completion.\r\n\r\nAvoid giant files.\r\n\r\nAvoid hidden magic constants.\r\n\r\nAvoid scattered animation timeouts.\r\n\r\nAvoid hardcoded Tall Tale IDs.\r\n\r\nAvoid hardcoded chapter order.\r\n\r\nAvoid assuming every content block uses exactly one page.\r\n\r\nAvoid assuming one Player per session.\r\n\r\nAvoid assuming the Captain is always connected.\r\n\r\nAvoid assuming all sessions begin at chapter one.\r\n\r\nAvoid assuming a completed Tall Tale can be reconstructed from the latest Creator version.\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n# 30. Documentation\r\n\r\nCreate or update project documentation explaining:\r\n\r\n* Player Library versus Player Session responsibilities\r\n* Canonical route structure\r\n* Journal component architecture\r\n* Session state model\r\n* Content block types\r\n* Captain and Player synchronization\r\n* Event model\r\n* Historical mode\r\n* Asset loading\r\n* Animation state machine\r\n* Accessibility behavior\r\n* Mobile behavior\r\n* Future vision-helper integration\r\n* Migration notes\r\n* Testing instructions\r\n\r\nAdd a clear architectural rule:\r\n\r\n> The Player Library is the place where Tall Tales are browsed. The immersive journal is the place where Tall Tales are played.\r\n\r\nInclude this rule in the relevant governing or source-of-truth documentation so future work does not accidentally replace the journal with cards again.\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n# 31. Future Vision Helper Compatibility\r\n\r\nThe architecture must remain ready for a future companion helper application that can observe gameplay and automatically verify locations, objects, scenes, or conditions.\r\n\r\nDo not implement the full computer-vision helper now unless it already exists in project scope.\r\n\r\nHowever, build trigger interfaces so that session progression can later receive events from:\r\n\r\n```text\r\nmanual Captain control\r\nPlayer confirmation\r\nrule engine\r\ntime-based trigger\r\nexternal helper application\r\nscreen vision service\r\nmachine-learning recognition\r\nlocation recognition\r\nobject recognition\r\nscene recognition\r\n```\r\n\r\nUse a generic verification event model.\r\n\r\nExample:\r\n\r\n```ts\r\ninterface VerificationEvent {\r\n  source:\r\n    | \"captain\"\r\n    | \"player\"\r\n    | \"system\"\r\n    | \"vision_helper\"\r\n    | \"external_service\";\r\n\r\n  verificationType:\r\n    | \"location\"\r\n    | \"object\"\r\n    | \"scene\"\r\n    | \"action\"\r\n    | \"manual\";\r\n\r\n  targetId: string;\r\n  confidence?: number;\r\n  evidence?: Record<string, unknown>;\r\n  createdAt: string;\r\n}\r\n```\r\n\r\nThe journal should react to verified events without caring whether the Captain or a future helper generated them.\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n# 32. Implementation Order\r\n\r\nUse a deliberate implementation sequence.\r\n\r\n## Stage 1: Investigation and Architecture\r\n\r\n* Locate existing journal implementation.\r\n* Map current routes.\r\n* Map current session data.\r\n* Identify card-based gameplay route.\r\n* Document intended migration.\r\n\r\n## Stage 2: Canonical Session Shell\r\n\r\n* Create shared Player session shell.\r\n* Connect active session route.\r\n* Render existing journal inside shell.\r\n* Restore current session position.\r\n\r\n## Stage 3: Content Rendering\r\n\r\n* Create typed block renderer.\r\n* Connect story, riddle, map, artifact, objective, and message blocks.\r\n* Preserve Creator block ordering.\r\n\r\n## Stage 4: Captain Synchronization\r\n\r\n* Connect release, verification, hint, artifact, chapter, and completion events.\r\n* Add reconnection and event replay protection.\r\n\r\n## Stage 5: Library Integration\r\n\r\n* Refactor cards to open correct journal sessions.\r\n* Add invitation, lobby, active, paused, and completed actions.\r\n* Remove competing gameplay card route.\r\n\r\n## Stage 6: Historical Mode\r\n\r\n* Add read-only completed journal.\r\n* Preserve session-version content.\r\n* Connect completed library cards.\r\n\r\n## Stage 7: Animation and Physical Polish\r\n\r\n* Fix page geometry.\r\n* Fix binding layers.\r\n* Fix page-turn stacking.\r\n* Improve cover, latch, seal, edges, and inserts.\r\n* Add session-aware entry animations.\r\n\r\n## Stage 8: Responsive and Accessibility\r\n\r\n* Add compact and single-page modes.\r\n* Add keyboard navigation.\r\n* Add reduced motion.\r\n* Add semantic reading order.\r\n\r\n## Stage 9: Testing and Documentation\r\n\r\n* Complete automated tests.\r\n* Run manual acceptance scenarios.\r\n* Update governing documentation.\r\n* Remove obsolete routes and dead code only after verification.\r\n\r\nDo not report the task complete after only routing the Player to the visual journal.\r\n\r\nThe journal must be connected to real Tall Tale session state and real content.\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n# 33. Completion Report\r\n\r\nWhen finished, provide a detailed report containing:\r\n\r\n1. Summary of the implementation\r\n2. Location of the journal code that was found\r\n3. Routes changed\r\n4. Components created\r\n5. Components reused\r\n6. Components retired\r\n7. Database changes\r\n8. API changes\r\n9. Session event changes\r\n10. Content block support\r\n11. Captain synchronization behavior\r\n12. Historical mode behavior\r\n13. Responsive behavior\r\n14. Accessibility behavior\r\n15. Tests added\r\n16. Tests run\r\n17. Build results\r\n18. Required Navigation Flow\r\n\r\nImplement a clear Player journey:\r\n\r\n```text\r\nRole Selection\r\n├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ Player Sign-In\r\n├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ Player Library\r\n├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ Select Tall Tale\r\n├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ Invitation or Lobby State\r\n├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ Enter Session\r\n├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ Immersive Journal Interface\r\n├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ Chapter Gameplay\r\n├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ Tall Tale Completion\r\n├óŌĆĀŌĆÖ Completed Journal Archive\r\n```\r\n\r\nThe application should support returning to the Player Library without destroying the active session.\r\n\r\nWhen the Player resumes, they should return to the correct journal state and page.\r\n\r\nRecommended route structure:\r\n\r\n```text\r\n/player\r\n/player/library\r\n/player/invitations\r\n\r\n/player/tall-tales/:tallTaleId\r\n/player/tall-tales/:tallTaleId/lobby\r\n\r\n/player/sessions/:sessionId\r\n/player/sessions/:sessionId/journal\r\n/player/sessions/:sessionId/map\r\n/player/sessions/:sessionId/artifacts\r\n/player/sessions/:sessionId/messages\r\n\r\n/player/history/:sessionId\r\n```\r\n\r\nThe exact route names may be adapted to the existing architecture, but the conceptual separation must remain.\r\n\r\nThe main Player session route should resolve to the immersive journal.\r\n\r\nFor example:\r\n\r\n```text\r\n/player/sessions/:sessionId\r\n```\r\n\r\nmay either directly render the journal or redirect to:\r\n\r\n```text\r\n/player/sessions/:sessionId/journal\r\n```\r\n\r\nDo not maintain multiple competing primary Player session interfaces.\r\n\r\nThere must be one canonical Tall Tale session shell.\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n# 4. Existing GM credentials and server-side sessions are shared by Captain and Creator capabilities. Existing Tall Tale Player sessions use an opaque random token whose hash is persisted and whose clear value is stored only in an HttpOnly cookie, but they do not yet provide a durable Player identity, library, invitation lifecycle, or multi-playthrough history selector.\n\n## Architecture decision\n\nThe platform implementation will extend the existing domain rather than introduce a disconnected replacement:\n\n- `TallTale` remains the authored identity.\n- `PublishedTaleVersion` remains the immutable release and historical rendering source.\n- `TaleSession` becomes the persisted playthrough aggregate. Existing preview-session behavior remains isolated through `previewMode`; every real new playthrough must reference one published version.\n- New Player profile/session, membership, invitation, invitation-event, reveal-state, scoped-role, and platform-audit records provide identity, library access, invitation lifecycle, revocation, and traceability.\n- Existing `GameMasterUser` credentials remain the strong account authority. Scoped role assignments supplement existing capability checks without invalidating current Captain/Creator logins.\n- Workspace-specific services return explicit Player-safe, Captain, and Creator view models. Raw Prisma entities and complete published snapshots are never serialized to Player library or invitation clients.\n- Existing `/tales`, `/play/[taleSlug]`, and `/captain` paths receive safe compatibility behavior while `/player/*`, `/join/*`, `/captain/library`, `/captain/invitations`, and `/studio/library` become the canonical platform families.\n\n## Migration and compatibility risks\n\n1. Existing `TaleSession` rows may already be active or completed. The migration must preserve their identifiers, access-token hashes, version binding, state, event order, inventory, variables, and timestamps.\n2. Legacy sessions do not have a durable Player profile or membership. Backfill must create deterministic guest profiles and memberships without changing their current runtime cookie behavior.\n3. Existing status values start at `ACTIVE`; new setup and invitation states must be accepted without breaking the progression engine, which may mutate only `ACTIVE` or `PAUSED` sessions and must keep `COMPLETED` terminal.\n4. Existing GM role/capability behavior must remain functional while explicit Captain and Creator denial is enforced on every new route and API.\n5. Published asset responses currently authorize by version identity. Player requests must additionally prove membership/session access and reveal scope; public-safe cover variants require a narrowly defined exception.\n6. SQLite is the supported local and test database, while a MySQL-parity migration must be maintained. The migration is additive and rollback is backup/restore plus application rollback; destructive down-migrations are not automated.\n7. The repository is public. Seeded accounts, invitations, story copy, names, PINs, and media remain fictional development data only.\n\n## Vertical implementation slices\n\n1. Add additive schema/migrations, domain state machines, authorization policies, token hashing, backfill, and development fixtures.\n2. Add secure Player session/sign-in, invitation resolution/acceptance/decline, library projection, waiting room, archive projection, and protected asset policy.\n3. Add Captain library, atomic playthrough/invitation creation, secure link/QR/short-code delivery, lifecycle management, launch synchronization, and audit history.\n4. Add the three-role cinematic gateway, role-aware sign-in and workspace switching, responsive Player/Captain screens, reduced-motion behavior, and compatibility redirects.\n5. Complete version comparison, restore/fork ancestry, immutable-release guards, authorization/concurrency tests, full role-journey browser coverage, migration validation, and documentation.\n\n## Completion evidence\n\nThe implementation is complete against the specification and is integrated with the existing Campaign, Quartermaster, and Tall Tale Studio domains.\n\n- Additive SQLite migration deployment succeeded from an empty validation database across all five repository migrations. A matching forward-only MySQL migration and schema were syntax-validated; a live MySQL service was not available in this workspace, so production MySQL deployment remains an operator-controlled rollout step with a verified backup.\n- The normal development seed created the platform foundation without resetting progress. A dedicated legacy-shaped playthrough proof then ran the same seed path and verified that the original playthrough ID, published-version binding, event history, timestamps, reveal history, and new membership all survived intact. A second seed after the complete browser journey preserved all accepted progress and backfilled zero additional playthroughs.\n- Static and unit gates passed: Prettier, ESLint, strict TypeScript, local animation assets, 25 Vitest files, and 80 unit/component tests.\n- The complete browser matrix passed 21 tests with 7 intentionally skipped mutation-heavy mobile permutations. Chromium exercised the full invitation-to-archive platform journey and the established Campaign, Command Center, animation, and Studio journeys. Mobile WebKit exercised protected access, the role gateway, reduced motion, responsive layouts, and accessibility.\n- Acceptance-state verification found 5 persisted playthroughs, 16 progression events, 18 legacy audit entries, and 14 platform audit events. It also proved immutable-version pinning, exact-version archive rendering, Player-safe projections, role/resource denial, CSRF enforcement, invitation replacement/revocation, idempotent acceptance, and per-membership archive preferences.\n- The optimized Next.js production build completed successfully, followed by two clean production start/health/stop cycles. `npm audit` reported zero known vulnerabilities after the dependency security updates.\n\nThe remaining deployment risks are operational rather than hidden implementation gaps: production secrets must replace development credentials, MySQL migration must be applied only after a backup in a maintenance window, persistent multi-instance rate limiting needs a shared backend, and uploaded assets need object storage plus malware scanning for multi-instance production. The implementation commit is `e469b12`; the subsequent path-scoped synchronization commit records this implementation document and the associated Codex transcript.\n\r\n---FILE:docs\\architecture.md---\r\n# Architecture\n\n## Phase 3 cinematic companion projection\n\nThe player reads one server-filtered `PublicSnapshot` containing chapters, released hints/annotations, visible map locations/routes, safe artifact states, visible optional mysteries, event-derived log entries, generic finale state, and per-section unseen counts. One SSE connection transports ordered sanitized events; section navigation is client-side and starts no independent polling.\n\nNew normalized records are `MapRoute` and `ViewedContent`. Existing content models gained release, relationship, placement, and safe-label fields rather than duplicating derived display tables. `AudioPreference` now carries the cross-device preference projection; immediate UI choices may also be cached locally for offline startup.\n\n```mermaid\nflowchart LR\n  P[Player journal + animation director] -->|snapshot + access cookie| N[Next.js server]\n  G[Quartermaster] -->|session + CSRF| N\n  N -->|Prisma transaction| D[(SQLite dev / MySQL prod)]\n  N -->|ordered SSE + replay| P\n  N --> A[Audit and save-state log]\n```\n\nServer Components enforce initial access. Route handlers own authentication, validation, snapshots, and SSE. `src/server/progression.ts` is the transaction boundary; `src/domain/story.ts` owns state rules. The UI receives only a public projection, never database rows. In-memory publish accelerates same-process delivery while database replay by sequence remains authoritative after reconnect/restart.\n\nThe client adds one animation director between ordered domain events and presentation. It starts server work immediately, allows only non-authoritative opening/idle motion while pending, and selects a success or failure timeline from the actual response. One queue owns SSE ceremonies, and the public snapshot remains authoritative after skip, cancellation, reconnect, or visual-runtime failure.\n\nMajor dependencies remain deliberately bounded: Prisma for persistence and transactions, bcryptjs for portable hashes, Zod for payload validation, GSAP for cinematic orchestration, Motion for React interaction/presence, StPageFlip for the journal surface, Rive/Lottie for isolated vector assets, Pino for structured redacted logs, and Vitest/Playwright for validation. See `docs/animation/architecture.md` and `docs/animation/library-ownership.md`.\n\nPhase 3 adds an administrative intent layer. `/api/gm/preview` projects without writes, `/api/gm/staging` persists unreleased intent, and `/api/gm/commands` enforces expected sequence and idempotency. `PlayerPresence` supplies expiring evidence. See [admin command pipeline](admin-command-pipeline.md) and [player presence](player-presence-and-sync.md).\n\n## Tall Tale Studio Phase 1\n\nStudio is additive to the original campaign companion. `TallTale` owns identity and catalog metadata; `TaleDraft` owns optimistic autosave state; chapters, blocks, and connections form the editable graph. Publishing validates that graph and writes a complete, checksummed `PublishedTaleVersion.contentSnapshot`. Published rows and referenced asset variants are immutable from the player runtime's perspective.\n\n`src/tall-tale/progression.ts` is the authoritative session engine. Each non-preview `TaleSession` is pinned to one published version and advances through idempotent, ordered events. The player receives its current projection and SSE updates; Captain actions call the same engine. Verification providers all enter through one versioned submission contract, so the simulator and a future paired helper cannot bypass progression rules. See `docs/tall-tale-studio.md`.\n\n## Unified Tall Tale Platform\n\nThe platform extends the Studio/session model rather than copying it. `PlayerProfile`/`PlayerIdentitySession` add durable Player identity; `PlaythroughMembership` is the per-Player authorization and library record; `Invitation`/`InvitationEvent` own single-recipient credential lifecycle; `RevealState` is the historical disclosure ledger; `PlatformRoleAssignment` supplements staff capability scope; and `PlatformAuditEvent` records correlated resource actions. `TaleSession` remains the one playthrough aggregate and retains the exact immutable version relation.\n\n`src/platform/auth.ts`, `policy.ts`, `state.ts`, `invitations.ts`, `libraries.ts`, and `audit.ts` separate authentication, policy, lifecycle, transactional invitation behavior, workspace-specific projections, and safe auditing. Player, Captain, and Creator route families call those services and never serialize a raw aggregate. Compatibility routes call the same progression engine. See [Tall Tale Platform](tall-tale-platform.md) for lifecycle, migration, and security detail.\n\r\n---FILE:docs\\tall-tale-platform.md---\r\n# Tall Tale Platform\n\n## Product surfaces\n\n`/` is a cinematic three-role gateway. Choosing Player, Captain, or Creator selects a workspace; it never grants a permission. Server sessions, capabilities, scoped assignments, playthrough membership, and exact resource ownership remain authoritative.\n\n- `/player/sign-in`, `/player/invitation`, `/player/library`, `/player/playthroughs/[id]`, and `/player/playthroughs/[id]/archive` provide durable Player identity, code/link acceptance, waiting state, live continuation, and historical records.\n- `/captain/sign-in`, `/captain/library`, `/captain/invitations`, `/captain/sessions/[id]`, and Player-safe preview routes provide operational voyage control without exposing Creator-only internals.\n- `/studio/sign-in`, `/studio/library`, and `/studio/tales/*` remain the authoring, validation, asset, version, fork, and publishing workspace.\n- `/tales`, legacy token sessions, `/quartermaster`, and the original companion remain compatibility surfaces.\n\nThe gateway may offer a remembered-session continuation, but every destination repeats authorization. Workspace switching links never upgrade the current account.\n\n## Domain and lifecycle\n\n`TallTale` is the authored identity. `PublishedTaleVersion` is an immutable checksummed snapshot. `TaleSession` is the playthrough aggregate and stores the exact `publishedVersionId`, Captain assignment, configuration, schedule, state, concurrency token, runtime pointers, inventory, and ordered events.\n\n`PlayerProfile` and rotating `PlayerIdentitySession` records provide durable identity. `PlaythroughMembership` associates each Player with one playthrough and carries invitation/ready/active/completed/declined/removed state plus per-Player pin/hide preferences. `Invitation` stores only token/code/PIN hashes and safe prefixes; `InvitationEvent` records lifecycle. `RevealState` records content actually revealed. `PlatformRoleAssignment` supplements existing staff capabilities. `PlatformAuditEvent` records resource actions with correlation IDs and secret-filtered metadata.\n\nSupported playthrough progression is `DRAFT_SETUP -> INVITING -> READY/SCHEDULED -> ACTIVE <-> PAUSED -> COMPLETED`, with cancellation before launch and abandonment after launch. Memberships move through invited, accepted, ready, active, and completed or terminate as declined/removed. Invitation links and codes move through created/sent/copied/viewed into ready/consumed, or terminate as declined/expired/revoked/replaced. Terminal transitions do not reopen in place.\n\n## Invitations and crew launch\n\nThe Captain wizard selects an exact published version, configures progression/hints/side quests/schedule/accessibility, adds one or more Players, chooses PIN/account/lifetime policy, reviews Player-safe content, and creates the playthrough plus all membership/invitation records in one transaction. Each crew member receives a distinct high-entropy link, QR code, human short code, and copyable message. Full secrets are returned only by creation or replacement responses and are never listed again.\n\nLink and code resolution is rate-limited. The pending invitation is held in a short-lived HttpOnly SameSite cookie with its own CSRF token. Acceptance atomically claims one redemption, binds or creates the Player identity, readies membership, records invitation/audit events, and readies the playthrough only when no invitation remains pending. Safe retries of an already accepted credential return the existing membership. Expired, declined, revoked, and replaced credentials are rejected before protected content is rendered. Account-required invitations can target only an existing claimed Player and must be accepted while signed into that exact profile.\n\nLaunch requires an assigned Captain, a ready/scheduled playthrough, at least one ready Player, the expected concurrency version, and a playable entry block. It promotes ready memberships, consumes accepted invitations, appends ordered launch/block events, records reveal state, and pushes sanitized realtime progression. The waiting room polls canonical state as a fallback and opens the runtime only after persisted launch.\n\n## Projection and authorization rules\n\nPlayer projections are allowlists. They contain current Player-safe Tale copy, revealed blocks/assets, crew readiness, and exact edition metadata; accepted answers, Captain instructions, Creator notes, future branches, private variables, storage keys, and raw event payloads are removed. Completed archives are rebuilt from the pinned published snapshot plus visited events/reveal state, not from the current draft or latest release.\n\nMedia reads require one of four explicit scopes: authenticated Creator asset management; Player membership in the exact version-bound playthrough plus reveal/role inclusion; pending invitation cover access; or the current public catalog cover. Original downloads require asset-management permission. SSE authenticates before streaming and periodically rechecks membership, emitting an access-revoked close signal when authorization changes.\n\nAll cookie-authenticated staff and Player mutations require CSRF, except legacy compatibility runtime cookies whose SameSite boundary and opaque session token are retained. Login, invitation-code lookup, Player actions, uploads, and helper endpoints are bounded by rate limits. Identity and invitation secrets are cryptographically random, stored only as hashes, sent through HttpOnly Secure-in-production cookies where applicable, and rotated/revoked on session replacement or logout. Audit metadata rejects secret-, answer-, snapshot-, payload-, and private-note-bearing fields.\n\n## Migration, backfill, and rollback\n\nSQLite migration `20260718020000_tall_tale_platform` and MySQL migration `0004_tall_tale_platform` are additive. They add platform fields and tables without rebuilding `TaleSession`, so existing IDs, version bindings, event sequences, access hashes, inventory, variables, and timestamps remain intact. The progress-preserving seed path creates missing development Player/staff assignments and backfills only non-preview sessions without memberships. Each gets a placeholder Player membership mapped from the existing session state, a voyage/launch value derived from existing fields, and block reveal records derived from historical `blockEntered` events. It does not reset campaign or Tall Tale progress.\n\n`scripts/verify-platform-backfill.ts` creates a legacy-shaped proof row in the disposable validation database, runs normal `--ensure`, then proves identity, event, version, membership, reveal, and timestamp preservation. `scripts/verify-database.ts` additionally checks published checksums, scoped development roles, membership coverage, exact version relations, and audit metadata.\n\nThere is no destructive down migration. Before production migration, back up the database and asset volume and verify restore. Rollback is application rollback plus restoration of that matched backup. The MySQL SQL is maintained for production parity, but a live MySQL integration environment is still required before production rollout.\n\n## Validation\n\nUnit tests cover playthrough/membership/invitation state rules, scoped authorization, and audit redaction. The Chromium mutation journey forks and publishes a Tale, creates and accepts an invitation, denies cross-role access and missing CSRF, launches, publishes a newer edition, proves the live session remains pinned, completes the Tale, validates the exact-version archive, persists pin/hide preferences, proves idempotent acceptance, and verifies replacement/revocation. The reduced-motion responsive gateway and authorization denials also run as a read-only mobile WebKit check. The repository release gate remains `npm run validate`.\n\r\n---FILE:docs\\journal-system.md---\r\n# Journal system\n\nChapters use `LOCKED`, `TEASER`, `READY`, `REVEALING`, `ACTIVE`, `SOLVED`, and `COMPLETE`. Locked/ready chapters serialize only ordinal, state, and an explicitly safe teaser. Narrative, objective, clue, released hints, annotations, and cross-links serialize only for readable states.\n\nHints are ordered records with a nullable release time. The server omits unreleased hints. Viewed state uses the player access identity and stable content keys, so it reconciles across devices that share the invitation identity. Annotations are released `JournalEntry` records and never include GM audit metadata.\n\n`buildJournalPages` converts only the sanitized public snapshot into stable physical page IDs: hard covers, endpapers, title/dedication, chapter dividers, readable narrative/objective/riddle leaves, sealed locked leaves, and back matter. StPageFlip receives selectable semantic HTML, updates its existing instance with `updateFromHtml`, preserves safe current indices, emits orientation/page events, and is destroyed on unmount. Keyboard buttons and Arrow/Page keys turn pages. Reduced motion renders the same page model without page curl.\n\nTo add a page type, extend the discriminated page model and its secret-filtering/index-stability tests, render one semantic copy in `JournalWorkspace`, and keep its ID based on stable public keys. See `docs/animation/architecture.md`.\n\r\n---FILE:docs\\player-companion-information-architecture.md---\r\n# Player Companion information architecture\n\nThe companion has six URL-addressable sections: `journal`, `chart`, `treasures`, `quests`, `log`, and `finale`. The selected section is stored in the `section` query parameter so refresh, deep links, back/forward navigation, and mobile/desktop handoff share one model. A persistent objective links back to the active journal chapter.\n\n```mermaid\nflowchart LR\n  O[Current objective] --> J[Journal]\n  J <--> C[Voyage chart]\n  J <--> T[Treasure altar]\n  J <--> Q[Side-quest ledger]\n  C <--> Q\n  T --> F[Sealed finale]\n  J --> L[Ship's log]\n  C --> L\n  T --> L\n  Q --> L\n  L --> J\n  L --> C\n  L --> T\n  L --> Q\n  L --> F\n```\n\nAll sections are projections of one authenticated public snapshot and one ordered SSE stream. Navigation never fetches hidden content and never starts a second polling loop.\n\nDesktop uses an artifact-like section rail and layered workspace. iPhone uses the same semantic navigation as a safe-area-aware bottom strip and one-column content. Locked links may navigate only to a safe locked state; they never cause protected payloads to be requested.\n\r\n---FILE:docs\\story-state-machine.md---\r\n# Story state machine\n\n## Companion sub-state\n\nChapter transitions remain authoritative. Map, route, artifact, side-quest, and finale state changes are separate domain events projected into the same campaign snapshot. They never bypass chapter visibility. New event types include route reveal, artifact silhouette/connection, quest completion, annotation/log arrival, and finale tease/requirement changes. Undo captures every mutable companion subsystem before applying a progression action.\n\n```mermaid\nstateDiagram-v2\n  LOCKED --> TEASER\n  LOCKED --> READY\n  TEASER --> READY\n  READY --> REVEALING\n  REVEALING --> ACTIVE\n  ACTIVE --> SOLVED\n  SOLVED --> COMPLETE\n  READY --> LOCKED: undo\n  ACTIVE --> READY: undo\n  SOLVED --> ACTIVE: undo\n```\n\nThe schema stores state and ordered immutable events rather than a chapter number alone. The vertical slice releases READY directly to durable ACTIVE in one transaction so animation failure never blocks truth; REVEALING is a client ceremony phase and remains available for future server acknowledgements. Every mutation saves a restore point, increments a campaign sequence, creates an event/snapshot/audit record, then publishes after commit. Event IDs plus device ceremony acknowledgements provide idempotency.\n\nAdministrative clients cannot set state directly. They submit named commands with an expected sequence. Pause blocks progression except resume, undo, and diagnostics. Ordered hints, unique awards, side-quest transitions, and chapter transitions are server-validated.\n\r\n---FILE:docs\\player-presence-and-sync.md---\r\n# Player presence and synchronization\n\n```mermaid\nsequenceDiagram\n  participant P as Player browser\n  participant S as Server\n  participant D as Database\n  participant G as Command Center\n  P->>S: heartbeat: device, route, visibility, acknowledged sequence\n  S->>D: upsert PlayerPresence\n  G->>S: GET status\n  S->>D: load evidence and campaign sequence\n  S-->>G: state, devices, last seen, lag\n```\n\nConnected means a non-disconnected heartbeat within 45 seconds. Recently lost means evidence within 120 seconds. Older evidence is stale; no evidence is unknown. A connected transport is never labeled ├óŌé¼┼ōviewed.├óŌé¼┬Ø Synchronized requires an active device whose acknowledged sequence equals the campaign sequence. Future production maintenance should expire records older than 30 days.\n\r\n---FILE:docs\\future-vision-helper.md---\r\n# Future vision helper boundary\n\nPhase 1 does not perform image recognition. It prepares a narrow, auditable provider seam so a later phone/helper implementation cannot become a second progression engine.\n\n## Reference preparation\n\nCreators can organize assets into location or artifact collections, including positive and negative reference sets, and assign a collection to a location. Locations retain a JSON verification profile for future provider configuration. Published snapshots freeze those records and referenced asset variants with the rest of a release.\n\n## Pairing\n\nAn authenticated Captain creates a short-lived pairing through `POST /api/helper/pair` with `sessionId` and a stable local `deviceId`. The server permits only active, published, non-preview sessions, stores a hash of the token, and returns the raw bearer token once. Tokens expire after 15 minutes. `GET /api/helper/status` acts as the scoped heartbeat: it updates presence and returns only session status, the pinned published version, current block, and current verification request. A Captain can revoke a device immediately through `DELETE /api/helper/pair/[pairingId]`; revocation is recorded as an ordered session event.\n\nPhase 1 intentionally provides the API boundary rather than a camera UI. A future QR or numeric-code ceremony should transmit the returned token over an authenticated local channel, avoid query-string logging, and rotate/revoke on re-pair.\n\n## Verification envelope\n\nThe helper submits `POST /api/helper/verification` with `Authorization: Bearer <pairing token>` and a versioned body:\n\n```json\n{\n  \"schemaVersion\": 1,\n  \"eventId\": \"provider-unique-event\",\n  \"idempotencyKey\": \"provider-stable-retry-key\",\n  \"eventType\": \"verification.observation\",\n  \"providerType\": \"visionLocation\",\n  \"providerInstanceId\": \"helper-device-id\",\n  \"sessionId\": \"session-id\",\n  \"publishedVersionId\": \"published-version-id\",\n  \"blockId\": \"current-block-id\",\n  \"verificationRequestId\": \"pending-request-id\",\n  \"observedAt\": \"2026-07-17T20:00:00.000Z\",\n  \"result\": \"match\",\n  \"confidence\": 0.92,\n  \"evidence\": { \"referenceCollectionId\": \"collection-id\" }\n}\n```\n\nThe API validates shape, bounds confidence to 0..1, updates pairing presence, applies a token-keyed rate limit without logging the token, and calls the same `submitVerification` function used by other providers. The engine binds the event to the pending request and checks session, published version, current block, provider type, and request status before advancing. Duplicate retries return the prior accepted result; contradictory or stale submissions are rejected and retained as verification evidence where appropriate. The helper never receives an unrestricted advance, jump, rollback, or Captain action endpoint.\n\n## Simulator\n\n`POST /api/captain/simulate` is development-only and requires a Captain session plus CSRF. It creates the same envelope and enters the same progression function with `sourceType=simulator`; it is not a shortcut or a production provider. The Captain session screen exposes match, no-match, and uncertain controls when a compatible request is pending.\n\n## Later implementation rules\n\n- Keep frame capture and model inference outside the authoritative web process.\n- Upload derived evidence by default, not raw frames; define retention and consent before storing imagery.\n- Sign provider releases and identify the provider instance/model in evidence.\n- Calibrate confidence per verification profile; never interpret confidence alone as permission to progress.\n- Preserve human Captain override and complete audit events.\n- Add a polished pairing/revocation ceremony and encrypted device-to-server transport before real-device rollout; the scoped heartbeat, API revocation, and process-local rate guards already exist.\n- Test false positive, false negative, duplicate, delayed, reordered, wrong-version, and offline/reconnect cases against the current contract suite.\n\r\n---FILE:docs\\responsive-behavior.md---\r\n# Responsive behavior\n\n## Complete shell\n\nDesktop uses the available monitor as a layered story workspace with persistent one-action navigation and compact objective access. Mobile switches to a single content column, labeled bottom navigation, safe-area padding, separate section views, and a compact return-to-clue control. The map always has a text alternative. Artifact inspection becomes a full-screen sheet on narrow screens. Fullscreen mode removes secondary chrome without removing navigation or the objective.\n\nAbove 1100px, chart, open journal, and relic display form a three-region physical workspace. At 1100px and below, bottom navigation exposes one view at a time. At 650px, the journal becomes one vertically readable parchment sheet with safe-area-aware bottom controls. Short phone landscape hides the spine/left sheet and uses a compact single-page composition. Capability choices use CSS width, height, orientation, hover-independent controls, safe-area insets, and `prefers-reduced-motion`; no user-agent sniffing is used.\n\nValidated viewports: 1920├āŌĆö1080, 1440├āŌĆö900, 390├āŌĆö844, 430├āŌĆö932, and 844├āŌĆö390. 2560├āŌĆö1440 was layout-reviewed through the same capped workspace rules; automated retained capture remains next-pass work.\n\r\n---FILE:docs\\testing.md---\r\n# Testing\n\nRun the complete release gate with:\n\n```powershell\nnpm run validate\n```\n\n## Complete validation gate\n\nThe command creates a clean local runtime and disposable database, then runs Prisma generation/migration/seed, database invariants, Prettier, ESLint, TypeScript, the complete Vitest suite, the Chromium/WebKit browser matrix, post-acceptance database checks, production build, and two production restart proofs.\n\nThe live workflow covers player/GM access, rate limiting, cookie isolation, prepare without disclosure, SSE release, ceremony timing/replay/preferences, persistence, duplicate rejection, award/map/solve/undo, offline pause/resume reconciliation, and heartbeat. That runtime receives only the current block and presents it as one centered `runtime-block` card. Its cards are correctly grouped by invitation, waiting, active/paused, completed, replay, and closed states. The accepted-invitation waiting room at `/player/playthroughs/[playthroughId]` is also correctly separated from active play.\n+\n+## Existing data and synchronization\n+\n+`TallTale`, `TaleDraft`, chapters, story blocks, and immutable `PublishedTaleVersion.contentSnapshot` already form one Creator/runtime content model. `TaleSession` is the version-pinned playthrough aggregate. Captain controls and helper verification both call the same progression engine.\n+\n+The current Player session API safely authenticates both durable Player memberships and legacy opaque runtime cookies, but it projects only the current block. Its block shape also includes more authoring structure than an immersive Player renderer requires. The archive API correctly rebuilds released history from the session's pinned published version, but it uses a competing visual surface.\n+\n+## Reuse, retirement, and route changes\n+\n+Reusable:\n+\n+- `PageFlipBook` and its reduced-motion fallback\n+- physical cover, page, binding, stack, latch, seal, and responsive CSS\n+- explicit journal-opening phase machine\n+- immutable published snapshots and the existing 23-type Creator block registry\n+- version-pinned `TaleSession`, reveal ledger, inventory, verification requests, durable events, SSE replay, and Captain progression controls\n+- Player Library cards and invitation/waiting-room flows\n+\n+Retired from primary Player gameplay after verification:\n+\n+- the one-card-at-a-time use of `PlayerRuntime`\n+- the standalone list-based use of `VoyageArchive`\n+\n+`PublishedBlockView` remains an isolated Studio block-preview renderer; it will no longer be the active Player session surface.\n+\n+Canonical route plan:\n+\n+- `/player/library` remains the card library.\n+- `/player/playthroughs/[playthroughId]` remains the invitation/lobby/waiting route and forwards launched or completed playthroughs into the journal.\n+- `/player/playthroughs/[playthroughId]/journal` becomes the durable-identity live and historical journal route.\n+- `/play/[taleSlug]/session/[sessionId]` remains a legacy compatibility route but renders the same canonical journal component.\n+- `/player/playthroughs/[playthroughId]/archive` becomes a compatibility redirect to the same historical journal instead of a second Player experience.\n+\n+## Implementation architecture\n+\n+The implementation will add a typed journal presentation contract over the existing canonical `PublishedBlock` data rather than copying Creator content. A Player-safe journal projection will expose only revealed blocks, safe presentation metadata, current/complete progress, authorized assets, and exact edition metadata. Logic-only blocks remain durable in the event stream but do not become visible pages.\n+\n+One reusable physical book frame will serve both the original campaign journal and the Tall Tale runtime. A Tall Tale page model will convert released blocks into stable page IDs and explicit story, riddle, map/location, artifact, decision, objective/waiting, message, cinematic/media, and completion page modes. Active and historical sessions use the same renderer; historical mode disables mutations and continues reading from the pinned immutable version.\n+\n+Canonical progress remains in `TaleSession`, `RevealState`, verification records, inventory, variables, and ordered events. Per-Player reading position and journal UI preferences will be persisted separately through the existing Player preference record, so browsing an older page never mutates the current block. Legacy cookie sessions use a local reading-state fallback only and do not change canonical progress.\n+\n+SSE remains the only live transport. Replayed event sequences refresh canonical state but do not replay already acknowledged visual triggers. A newly released current block physically turns the journal only when the Player is following live progress; otherwise the journal announces new content and offers a Return to Current Objective action.\n+\n+No AR/Vision Waypoint Phase B1 documents or implementation files are part of this change. The two pre-existing untracked Phase B PDFs are protected parallel work and must not be edited, staged, or committed by this task.\n+\n+## Validation plan\n+\n+- unit tests for the journal contract, recursive secret filtering, block-to-page mapping, stable IDs, page parity, historical mode, and current-objective indexing\n+- component tests for page-turn locking, keyboard/reduced-motion behavior, and canonical journal actions\n+- browser coverage for library-to-journal routing, waiting-to-live transition, reload restoration, Captain-driven progression, completed historical journal, authorization, responsive layouts, and accessibility\n+- full `npm run validate`, followed by the repository's required conversation/development-document synchronization gate\n*** End Patch";

setOpeningPhase(\"JOURNAL_READY\");\n+    saveReading({ hasOpened: true });\n+  }\n+\n+  function turnTo(page: number) {\n+    book.current?.flipTo(page);\n+    saveReading({ openDrawer: null });\n+  }\n+\n+  function returnToCurrent() {\n+    if (!state) return;\n+    const page = pageIndexForJournalBlock(pages, state.journal.currentBlockId);\n+    followingCurrent.current = true;\n+ Its block shape also includes more authoring structure than an immersive Player renderer requires. The archive API correctly rebuilds released history from the session's pinned published version, but it uses a competing visual surface.\n\n## Reuse, retirement, and route changes\n\nReusable:\n\n- `PageFlipBook` and its reduced-motion fallback\n- physical cover, page, binding, stack, latch, seal, and responsive CSS\n- explicit journal-opening phase machine\n- immutable published snapshots and the existing 23-type Creator block registry\n- version-pinned `TaleSession`, reveal ledger, inventory, verification requests, durable events, SSE replay, and Captain progression controls\n- Player Library cards and invitation/waiting-room flows\n\nRetired from primary Player gameplay after verification:\n\n- the one-card-at-a-time use of `PlayerRuntime`\n- the standalone list-based use of `VoyageArchive`\n\n`PublishedBlockView` remains an isolated Studio block-preview renderer; it will no longer be the active Player session surface.\n\nCanonical route plan:\n\n- `/player/library` remains the card library.\n- `/player/playthroughs/[playthroughId]` remains the invitation/lobby/waiting route and forwards launched or completed playthroughs into the journal.\n- `/player/playthroughs/[playthroughId]/journal` becomes the durable-identity live and historical journal route.\n- `/play/[taleSlug]/session/[sessionId]` remains a legacy compatibility route but renders the same canonical journal component.\n- `/player/playthroughs/[playthroughId]/archive` becomes a compatibility redirect to the same historical journal instead of a second Player experience.\n\n## Implementation architecture\n\nThe implementation will add a typed journal presentation contract over the existing canonical `PublishedBlock` data rather than copying Creator content. A Player-safe journal projection will expose only revealed blocks, safe presentation metadata, current/complete progress, authorized assets, and exact edition metadata. Logic-only blocks remain durable in the event stream but do not become visible pages.\n\nOne reusable physical book frame will serve both the original campaign journal and the Tall Tale runtime. A Tall Tale page model will convert released blocks into stable page IDs and explicit story, riddle, map/location, artifact, decision, objective/waiting, message, cinematic/media, and completion page modes. Active and historical sessions use the same renderer; historical mode disables mutations and continues reading from the pinned immutable version.\n\nCanonical progress remains in `TaleSession`, `RevealState`, verification records, inventory, variables, and ordered events. Per-Player reading position and journal UI preferences will be persisted separately through the existing Player preference record, so browsing an older page never mutates the current block. Legacy cookie sessions use a local reading-state fallback only and do not change canonical progress.\n\nSSE remains the only live transport. Replayed event sequences refresh canonical state but do not replay already acknowledged visual triggers. A newly released current block physically turns the journal only when the Player is following live progress; otherwise the journal announces new content and offers a Return to Current Objective action.\n\nNo AR/Vision Waypoint Phase B1 documents or implementation files are part of this change.
